Famous Painting Stolen in Brussels: The Work of a 15th-Century Painter; Returned After Being Stipulated by Treaty 42

The Saint Bavo Cathedral in Ghent, Belgium, is one of the most famous cathedrals in Belgium. The interior walls are made of marble, and the altarpiece is composed of three famous paintings by the Van Eyck brothers, 15th-century painters, entitled "Adoration of the Mystic Lamb." The three paintings were previously placed in three different locations: one in Ghent, one in Brussels, and one in Berlin. But the Treaty of Versailles stipulated that the Berlin painting be returned to Belgium, so the three paintings were restored to one place. The church verger would lower a curtain over them every night and roll it up the next morning. Today, when the verger rolled up the curtain, he found that one of the paintings had disappeared. The thief must have hidden in the church when the door was locked at night and stolen the priceless painting. The stolen painting is 37 inches high and 19 inches wide, depicting "Justice" with an image of John. (Reuters dispatch on the 11th)

Disarmament Conference Reopens on May 23; Executive Committee to Hold Second Meeting at the End of the Month 43

Eden Indicates British Plan is Amendable

Diplomatic Negotiations Must Continue

(Geneva) The Steering Committee of the Disarmament Conference decided today that May 23 will be the confirmed date for the General Commission of the Disarmament Conference. April 30 will be the date for the next meeting of the Steering Committee. The Chairman of the Disarmament Conference, Henderson, has the authority to postpone the dates of the two meetings if he deems it necessary. British Lord Privy Seal Eden suggested that the Steering Committee should meet on April 30 in order to continue direct negotiations. Eden said, "If a disarmament convention is to be established, it should be done as soon as possible, because a convention recording disarmament is worth our efforts today." Eden continued, "The British proposal can be amended again, but the

delays caused by changing circumstances are of the utmost concern to Britain." Subsequently, Soviet representative Stein stated that the Soviet Union is prepared to accept any disarmament convention, but it must be conditioned on the unanimous acceptance of the Soviet Union's neighbors. Stein also suggested that the Disarmament Conference should pay special attention to the non-aggression pact initiated by President Roosevelt based on the Soviet-defined aggressor boundaries. If the Steering Committee of the Disarmament Conference can convene on April 30, it will draft a new disarmament convention based on the points of agreement negotiated since last October. (National Telegram on the 10th)

Countries Declare Opinions at Disarmament Steering Committee; Reopening Date Temporarily Decided; British-French Negotiations Continue 44

(Geneva) The Bureau of the Disarmament Conference met at 3:30 PM and decided that the Bureau would meet on April 30, and the General Commission would be convened around May 23.

However, Chairman Henderson may advance or postpone the date as appropriate depending on the negotiation situation. A detailed telegram reports other speeches made by various parties at today's meeting. Here is a brief explanation of the intentions expressed by each

party: 1) The representatives of Soviet Russia, Poland, and Sweden strongly stated that the purpose of the Disarmament Conference is to reduce armaments, not just to limit armaments. 2) The representatives of Belgium and Italy believe that the ongoing diplomatic talks are more promising, so they believe that although a date for the General Commission is scheduled, it is futile to set a date unless there is certainty that all parties agree. 3) The words of the British representative Eden are sufficient to represent the concerns of the delegation and deserve our attention. Eden advocated for "swift action," saying that Britain

is well aware that the facts in Germany are very dangerous to peace. 4) The French representative Massigli expressed sympathy with Eden on this point. In short, today's meeting was conducted in an atmosphere of sincerity and clarity. Tomorrow, Eden, Massigli, Belles, and other representatives attending the meeting will hold a closed-door meeting to exchange views to await the results of the Paris-London diplomatic talks. (Havas dispatch on the 10th)

(Geneva) The general situation at today's meeting of the Bureau of the Disarmament Conference has been noted in a previous telegram. Here are the detailed speeches of Chairman Henderson and the representatives: 1) Henderson advocated convening the General Commission on May 23 and said that almost all major countries are increasing their military budgets. The disarmament competition has restarted and continues to this day. Some public opinion believes that the situation is hopeless, and these people clearly despise the meaning of disarmament, intending that countries should act independently regarding armaments and return to the previous chaotic international situation, with each holding strong armor and sharp weapons to confront each other. Henderson concluded by urging countries to cooperate sincerely, based on existing treaties and previously agreed principles, to establish a disarmament convention so that the new trend of military competition can be stopped and the ever-expanding danger of war can be avoided. 2) The British representative, Eden, advocated that the Bureau postpone the meeting until April 30 so that he could carefully examine the situation and express his views on the level of confirming the reopening of the General Commission. Eden said that the opinions of France and Germany on various issues differed greatly. For example, regarding the calculation of military quotas, it is still difficult to reach agreement on colonial troops, trained reserves, and military groups other than formal troops. Also, German short-term conscript troops must go through a certain trial period before they can be equipped with defensive

weapons, but when this trial period begins and how long it lasts are points that are difficult to agree on. In view of the various difficulties, Eden advocated postponing the meeting of the Bureau to allow diplomatic negotiations to continue. 3) The Soviet representative Stein spoke after Henderson and Eden, saying that as long as disarmament is universal, the Soviet Union is happy to accept any reduction in existing armaments. So-called universal disarmament means that all countries, without distinction, implement disarmament uniformly. Stein believed that the Disarmament Conference should study one: the Soviet proposal regarding the definition of aggressor countries, two: the French proposal regarding security, and three: the US President's proposal regarding non-aggression treaties. 4) The French representative Massigli spoke next, reiterating the main principles advocated by the Disarmament Conference before Germany's withdrawal from the Disarmament Conference on October 14, 1933, and said that various new facts have emerged at present, and the most important of them is Germany's request to immediately reorganize the disarmament plan in quality and quantity. Massigli said that Germany's reply to France on March 13 of this year, on the one hand, requested permission for Germany to immediately reorganize its armaments, and on the other hand, requested other countries to reduce their armaments. This attitude is inevitably contradictory. Massigli believed that Germany's proposal was tantamount to fundamentally overturning the basis of the discussions at the Disarmament Conference, and if this was to be done, the General Commission must be convened to vote on it, because only the General Commission has the power to decide whether the principles on which the Disarmament Conference has been based in the past should be abandoned. Massigli then said that Germany is actually engaged in reorganizing its armaments, so the question remains as to how much the difference between its demands and the actual situation of its armaments is. The French representative continued that the British government is working hard to study the issue of guarantees for the implementation of the disarmament convention in order to make it clearer. The French government is very grateful and firmly believes that it will soon be able to agree with London to find a solution. Massigli concluded by saying that the French government will do its best to bring about a general conclusion to the situation as soon as possible so that it can report to the Disarmament Conference. 5) Swedish Foreign Minister Sandtler, Swiss representative Motta, and Polish representative Lecinski spoke one after another, all hoping to obtain concrete results. Sandtler especially advocated three points, namely (a) substantive disarmament, (b) appropriate implementation of the ○ principle of equality in disarmament, and (c) the establishment of new security guarantees. Motta said that he believes that Germany must be ordered to return to Geneva, because without Germany, the disarmament convention cannot be discussed in spirit. Lecinski agreed with the French representative's opinion. (Havas dispatch on the 10th)

German Factories Relocating to Britain: Secret Negotiations Underway 47

(London) Britain and Germany are currently engaged in secret negotiations to discuss the relocation of eighteen major German textile factories to Britain. This is a rare migration movement in recent years. It is said that Germany's policy of mistreating Jews has sparked a global boycott of the National Socialist Party and German-produced goods. Moreover, German manufacturers are unable to purchase foreign currency for exchanging foreign-produced raw materials. Consequently, the idea of relocating factories has emerged. Representatives of German industrialists are currently selecting factory sites in Britain and hope that the British government will approve the relocation. The factories involved in the relocation primarily manufacture women's clothing, and their total foreign trade amounts to approximately two million marks annually. Recently, due to the boycott of the National Socialist Party by various countries, they have suffered a severe decline. German manufacturers firmly believe that the "Made in Britain" label will avoid foreign boycotts and enable German foreign trade to recover. The German government has unexpectedly expressed approval, believing that this is the only solution for rescuing the factories in question. Managers of the factories involved have promised the German government to purchase a certain amount of raw materials from Germany annually and transport them to British factories for manufacturing. It is said that if the relocation continues unchanged and the outcome is successful, other German factories will follow suit, not just in the textile industry. (National Telegram, 10th)

Spaniard Injures Fascist Leader with Bomb 48

Madrid: The son of former Spanish dictator Rivera, currently a leader of the Spanish Fascists, was traveling through the city in a car today when someone threw two bombs at him. One bomb penetrated the car and exploded, lightly injuring Rivera with shrapnel. He immediately drew his gun and jumped out of the car. A crowd gathered, attempting to harm him, but police arrived shortly and dispersed the mob. (National Telegram, 11th)

Jesus' Resurrection Easter Egg 49

Costing £5,000 to Make, Sold for Only £85 (London) Today, Christie's auction house offered a gold Easter egg, made at a cost of £5,000, but it only fetched £85 at auction. The egg was presented to Russian Emperor Alexander III in 1886 by Fabergé, the world-renowned goldsmith who specialized in creating gold ornaments for European monarchs and queens. The eggshell is white enamel, with a mechanism inside that opens at a touch, revealing a gold yolk. Inside the yolk is a gold hen, multicolored, and inside the hen is an imperial crown, and inside the crown is a small egg of red benitoite. All can be unfolded layer by layer. The Russian Emperor loved this egg and ordered Fabergé to make one every year to present to his empress on Easter. (Reuters, 11th)

Ministry of Communications Urges Provinces to Abolish Parcel Post Tax 54

Nanjing: The Ministry of Communications has repeatedly ordered the abolition of parcel post taxes, but it has been found that Hunan, Yunnan, Guizhou, Guangdong, Guangxi, Shaanxi, Gansu, Xinjiang, Ningxia, Qinghai, Zhangjiakou, Duolun, Guihua, and Sichuan are still collecting taxes. The tax rates range up to 20% ad valorem, and some weigh over three yuan per item. The names of these fees are constantly changing, and inspection points are everywhere, which is no different from disguised likin. The complexity of the collection procedures and the amount of the tax are far greater than likin. If this continues, parcel post delivery will completely disappear. Whether it is for the welfare of the people or the future of the postal service, it is necessary to abolish it immediately. The Ministry of Communications urges the provinces to completely abolish it within this year. (Special Dispatch, 11th)

Shipping companies will hold a meeting to discuss and share the responsibility. The amount is yet to be determined. Measures for Refunding Original Wheat Tax on Exported Domestic Flour 75

Nanjing: At the request of Chinese flour mills, the Ministry of Finance has established three principles for refunding the original wheat import tax on exported flour: 1. The amount of the tax refund is limited to the amount of import tax actually paid by the flour mill for foreign wheat. 2. The percentage of Chinese and foreign wheat used by manufacturers to produce flour is not uniform. After wheat is made into flour, its form is completely changed, and it is impossible to distinguish between Chinese and foreign wheat. The submitted wheat import certificates can be approved for tax refund to facilitate customs enforcement. Due to the special preferential treatment of Chinese wheat, its sales can also be promoted. However, the tax refund should be reduced by 20% as compensation for tax refund procedures. 3. The tax refund will not be issued in cash but in the form of wheat tax payment certificates, which can only be used to offset wheat import taxes. (Special Dispatch, 11th)

Gold and Silver 99

London Gold Price: Today (11th), the London gold price is 134 shillings and 10.5 pence, up 4.5 pence.

London Silver Bar: Today (11th), the silver bar market is stable. Spot price is 20.125 pence, and the futures price is 20.375 pence, both the same as yesterday's price. Speculators bought and sold, but trading was not active. The market closed quiet and stable.

Bombay Silver Bar: Today (11th), the Bombay silver market closed steady. Spot price rose two annas to 55 rupees and eight annas.

New York Silver Bar: Today (11th), the silver market became more stable due to the Senate committee's passage of the Dies Act, but speculators' interest was not strong when the market opened. Speakers were skeptical about whether the Dies Act could become law. Subsequently, developments continued in Washington, and the market stabilized. It is widely believed that a new proposal of a more moderate nature will be made. Therefore, today's forward opening price is up 0.125 to 0.25 pounds compared to yesterday's closing price.

Exchange Rates 100

British and American: Today (the 11th), the London foreign exchange market opened with the British-American exchange rate at 5 yuan, 1 jiao, 6 fen and a half. This was the same as yesterday's closing price for the American-British exchange rate. The price gradually decreased in the morning. At 2:00 PM, the price was 5 yuan, 1 jiao and 6 fen, a drop of half a fen from the opening price. Also, one US dollar was equivalent to three shillings and ten and five-twelfths pence.

British and French: Today (the 11th), the opening price was 78 francs 25, a drop of three points from yesterday's closing price. It continued to decline, and the closing price was 78 francs 12.

American and British: Today (the 11th), the New York exchange rate for British pounds opened at 5 yuan, 1 jiao, 5 fen, 875. This was a drop of 625 from the previous day's closing price. The 23-group trading price remained unchanged. The fifth trading price rebounded and changed to 5 yuan, 1 jiao, 6 fen. The sixth trading price increased again to 5 yuan, 1 jiao, 6 fen, 125.

American and French: The New York exchange rate for French francs opened today at 6.60.25, the same as the previous day's closing price.

An Inspection Tour of Xinjiang by Our Special Correspondent, Geng Ya 105

The Route to Xinjiang

While waiting for internal permits in Pingyin, and after receiving a reply telegram from Xinjiang Province, I stayed for several days and visited Commissioner Zhu Jiqing, Chairman Song Zheyuan, and Director of Civil Affairs Qin Dechun, as well as several gentlemen from the press, Zhao Ximeng, Xu Maoxian, and Lang Xiaocang, and from the education sector, Chen Zhongyi, Wang Youdao, and Luo Ming. The main points of our discussions were: (1) The Japanese are implementing their Tanaka Doctrine thoroughly. The Northeast has already been seized, and the situation between Japan and Russia is tense again. The situation in North China is becoming increasingly dangerous. We lack strength and are finding it difficult to cope. (2) Given China's current situation, no matter from which perspective we view it, developing the Northwest is a crucial task. The sooner it is implemented, the better, as further delays may be irredeemable.

The Hui people of Gansu account for about half of the province's population. In Xinjiang Province, the Hui people make up 70 to 80 percent of the population. Before entering Xinjiang, I inquired about their customs. I specifically visited the "China Islamic Advancement Association" and met with Mr. Li Yunting and Mr. Ma Xingdong, the secretary of the Turkish Embassy.

They briefly stated, "In China's current precarious situation, the genuine cooperation of all five ethnic groups is barely enough to save the country. If they continue to harbor doubts and dissent, the future will be even more bleak." Mr. Xingdong, with his enthusiasm and sincerity, introduced me to Mr. Ma Songting, the principal of the Chen Da Normal School, who briefly explained the school's purpose and history: "Our school's purpose is to cultivate healthy teachers and promote Islam (the Hui religion). The expenses are covered by the board of directors' fundraising and we do not charge for board, lodging, or tuition. The reason for its establishment is that we, the same-minded people, realized the decline of our religion. Considering that we want to develop the religious teachings and improve the status of our religious people, we must first cultivate healthy teachers, organize the temple administration, and awaken the religious people. It is not enough to plan the overall progress of our Islamic nation. Therefore, we founded our school in Jinan in 1925, adopting the three-three system of normal schools, and started enrolling students. During this period, it was suspended twice due to the May 3rd Massacre, etc. After the same-minded people worked hard and with the strong support of Mr. Ma Hongkui, etc., school affairs were restored and developed daily. In 1929, the school site was moved to Beiping." Afterwards, I visited the auditorium, lecture hall, and dormitory, all of which were quite clean and tidy.

The most convenient route to Xinjiang is to take a plane from Beijing, via Xi'an, Lanzhou, and Hami, to Dihua, which takes three days and costs about 2,000 yuan. The next is to take the Xin-Sui long-distance bus from Ping to Sui, via Ulan Ali Gen, Hami, and Guchengzi, to Dihua. The entire line is 5,980 li (2,917 kilometers), takes 14 days, and costs 335 yuan. Food and lodging are provided by the bus. This road was originally a trade route, and it passes through hard Gobi deserts. Even if there is light sand, it is easy to handle. The road is flat and easy to travel, and it is quite appropriate to reconstruct it as a highway. Mule and camel transport takes at least 70 days (from Ping to Dihua). Supplies are difficult to obtain along the way, so the cost is lower than bus transport. The third route is to take the Siberian Railway. Currently, it is not possible to go directly from the Northeast. You must take a ship via Japan (because there are very few ships from Tianjin directly to Vladivostok), transfer to Vladivostok, and then take a train to Aigun, transfer to a bus, enter Tacheng, and reach Dihua, which takes more than 40 days and costs more than 400 yuan. The fourth route is to take the Longhai Railway, via Shaanxi, Gansu, and Hami, to Dihua, which takes about 80 days. From Hami to Dihua, if you do not take a car and walk with camels, it takes 20 days. In the winter and spring seasons, the climate is severely cold, so the

Southern route of Tianshan is taken, via Shanshan and Turpan. In the summer and autumn, the northern route of Tianshan is taken, passing through Muleihe and Qitai to reach Dihua. I do not wish to take the above routes by plane or detour through Siberia. The Xin-Sui long-distance bus has no buses going recently. In order to make a more detailed inspection along the way, I decided to take the Ping-Sui Railway to Baotou, transfer to Ningxia, and insert into the fourth route, and first detour to Qinghai before entering Xinjiang.

The Japanese Control of the Northeast Railway Establishes Four Management Bureaus 106

Important officials announced amidst reorganization, divided into six sections, fifteen departments, and forty-one units.

Changchun Correspondence: The Japanese built railways in the Northeast, completing the railway network, in order to facilitate military transportation and to defend against Russia and eliminate the Volunteer Army. However, although the railway network is completed, the internal organization is even more important. Therefore, the Japanese implemented a plan to control the Northeast Railway, adopting a four-bureau management system, dividing regions and allocating duties. It has been implemented since April 1st. The detailed organization and newly announced important personnel are listed below.

The Four-Bureau System 107

The names and locations of the four bureaus are as follows: (1) Fengtian Railway Management Bureau, located in Fengtian, managing 1,212 kilometers of the old Fengshan and Shenhai railway bureaus. (2) (Puppet) Xinjing Railway Management Bureau, located in the puppet capital, managing 781 kilometers of the old Jichang, Jidun, and Jihai bureaus. (3) Harbin Railway Management Bureau, located in Harbin, managing 327 kilometers of the old Huhai Bureau. (4) Taonan Railway Management Bureau, located in Taonan, managing 1,092 kilometers of the old Sitao, Taoang, and Taosuoqike bureaus. (Note: The Chaokai Line is under the jurisdiction of the puppet Xinjing Railway Bureau.)

Reorganization Names 108

The six sections, fifteen departments, and forty-one units after the reorganization are as above. General Affairs Section: Document Department, Personnel Department, Attached Property Department. Management Section: Accounting Department, Expenditure Department. Transportation Section: Passenger Department, Cargo Department. Mechanical Department: Operation Department, Work Department. Engineering Section: Engineering Department, Improvement Department, Electrical Department. Police Affairs Section: Line Affairs Department, Defense Department, Inspection Office.

Establishment of Offices 109

For the sake of convenience, the following offices have been established: Jin County Railway Office (under the jurisdiction of the Fengtian Railway Bureau), Tumen Railway Office (under the jurisdiction of the Xinjing Railway Bureau), and Sipingjie Railway Office (under the jurisdiction of the Taonan Railway Bureau). The organization of these offices includes five units: General Affairs, Transportation, Mechanical Affairs, Engineering, and Police.

Establishment of Water Transport Bureau 110

In order to facilitate combined water and land transport, a Water Transport Bureau has been established in Harbin, planning water transport and operating ancillary businesses. The bureau's organization is as follows: General Affairs Section: Subdivided into General Affairs, Police Affairs, Accounting, and Expenditure units. Business Section: Subdivided into Shipping and Wharf units. Engineering Section: Subdivided into Engineering and Shipbuilding units. It also manages the following agencies: (1) Harbin Wharf Business Office, (2) Fujin Wharf Business Office, (3) Heihe Wharf Business Office, (4) Harbin Shipyard, (5) Harbin Automobile Office.

Newly Ordered Lines 111

The newly revised lines are as follows: (1) Fengshan Line (Fengtian-Shanhaiguan), (2) Dazheng Line (Dahushan-Tongliao-Zhengjiatun), (3) Ying Line (Goubangzi-Yingkou), (4) Beipiao Line (Jin County-Beipiao), (5) Huludao Line (Lianshan-Huludao), (6) Fengji Line (Fengtian-Jilin), (7) Xi'an Line (Shahe-Xi'an), (8) Jingtumen Line (Xinjing-Tumen), (9) Naizishan Line (Jiaohe-Naizishan), (10) Chaokai Line (Chaoyangchuan-Kaishantun), (11) Binbei Line (Binjiang-Bei'an), (12) Machuankou Line (Xin Songpu-Machuankou), (13) Qibei Line (Qiqihar-Bei'an), (14) Nehe Line (Ningnian-Nehe), (15) Pingqi Line (Sipingjie-Qiqihar), (16) Taosuo Line (Taonan-Suolunshan), (17) Yushutun Line (Yushutun-Ang'angxi).

Key Officials 112

The key personnel of each bureau are as follows: Ota Hisaku (Japanese), former engineer of the Railway General Bureau, promoted to Director of the Fengtian Railway Management Bureau. Zhao Xinzhe, former chief of the Engineering Section of the Fengshan Railway Bureau, promoted to Deputy Director of the Fengtian Railway Management Bureau. Jin Bidong, former director of the Jichang and Jidun Railway Bureaus, promoted to Director of the Xinjing Railway Management Bureau. Yamamine Teiji (Japanese), former chief of the Engineering Section of the Railway General Bureau, promoted to Deputy Director of the Xinjing Railway Management Bureau. Zhou Peibing appointed Director of the Taonan Railway Management Bureau. Sakai Seibei (Japanese), former counselor of the Railway General Bureau, promoted to Deputy Director of the Taonan Railway Management Bureau. Ozawa Nobuyoshi (Japanese), former counselor of the Railway General Bureau, promoted to Director of the Harbin Railway Management Bureau and concurrently Director of the Harbin Water Transport Bureau. Wu Yingyuan, Deputy Director of the Shenyang Railway Bureau, transferred to Deputy Director of the Harbin Railway Management Bureau. Qian Suisun, former secretary of the Railway General Bureau, promoted to Counselor of the Railway General Bureau.

Newly Constructed Lines 113

The four lines being constructed by the Japanese in Jilin Province, which began construction in February of this year, are listed below: (1) Between the puppet Xinjing and Damasumu (western part of the former Gorlos Banner), totaling 225 kilometers in length. (2) Between Dongning and Ning'an, totaling 210 kilometers in length. (3) Between Shimenzi and Suihua, totaling 113 kilometers in length. (4) Between Haimi and Jilan, totaling 246 kilometers in length. All four lines are scheduled to be completed in July of this year. (Northeast News Agency)

Bandit Liu Breaks Through and Flees into Ju County 114

Most Fleeing Towards Fengshan

A Small Number Returning Near Xia Village

Seemingly Still Trying to Flee into Jiangsu Province

Jinan Correspondence: The remnants of Liu Guitang's bandits were heavily surrounded yesterday in the areas of Xiatangzhuang, Jiangyu, and Sijiaoquan in Yishui County. Realizing that the various suppression forces were gathering, the bandits desperately broke out in an attempt to escape. Yesterday, they first planned to break out from the north of Yanziyu, but were repelled by Sun Tongxuan's troops of the 20th Division, suffering considerable losses. Around 7:00 PM, as darkness fell and visibility was poor, the bandits merged a small force from Sijiaoquan into one unit, and broke through to the south with all their might. The southern side was met by Xie Shuxian's Lu Southern militia, but the bandits were extremely fierce, advancing one after another without retreating. Xie's militia were ultimately weaker than the regular army, and were broken through, with the bandits spilling blood and fleeing south. They passed through Xiangluzi Cliff, Fengjia Cliff, Longhu Ridge, Gao Ridge, Baijia Ridge, and Zhangzhuangzi to Luyouzhuang, fleeing overnight without stopping. Today (the 9th) at 11:00 AM, headquarters received a report from Zhaoxian Town that the bandits had crossed Yishui, turned east, and entered Ju County. Because they suffered heavy losses during the breakout, heavy objects were discarded everywhere as they fled in panic. At 8:00 AM, they arrived at Luozhuzhuang, and then fled southeast to Xinlipu, reaching Tiandiling (40 li from Ju County). As of 4:00 PM this afternoon, headquarters continued to receive reports that the bandits had passed Mulishui from San Shili Pu and turned north again, heading for Li Ziwang (north of Zhaoxian Town). Currently, Ma Guanyi's brigade is in pursuit, and other units are also blocking them from all sides.

Another dispatch: After the bandits broke out, they passed near Majia Cliff, Weizao Hutong, and Tangjia River, stealing and breaking through heavy encirclement, and fleeing into the territory of Ju County overnight. They passed through the south of Zheshui City for thirty to forty li, passing through Hushang, Huangshan, Zhujialou, Taipingzhuang, Yaodianzi, Daqiaopozizhuang, Qianchengzi Wujiazhuang, Zhujiazhuang, Miaojiazhuang, Chengziji Quanliguanzhuang, Yuanjiazhuang Anzi, Xiajiaqiao Liujiazhuang, Nanshezhuang, Qiuzhuang, all the way to the Simadianzi area, which is directly south of Yishui City. The bandits were divided into two groups, the large group fled northeast from the south of Yongshan (south of Yishui City), entered the central part of Ju County, passed Wangjial, Duwa, Yinglingshan, Liuling, along the south of the Yellow River, passed Mazhuang Xiaowo, Lijiazhuang, Hujiazhuang, Mazhuang, Jialaiwang Lianzi Hutong, Huliugou, Yujiahe, Zhang Haizi Hou Kezhuang, Daguanzhuang, Jiaojiazhuang, Kangguan, passed Xueshan, passed Shang Yai Xia Yai, Huiquan Shankou, Zhujia Gou, to Luozhuzhuang, thirty-odd li north of Ju County City, at 8:00 AM yesterday (the 9th), and again passed through the front and rear Si Dun, Zhangzhuang, Sunkongzhuang, Qiuguazhuang, Beiwenzhuang, Zhoujiazhuang, Suguanzhuang, crossed the Shuh River, and then passed through Hedongzhuang, Jiajiazhuang, Lujiazhuang, Shiluguanzhuang, and had already reached Maopu Town by noon. In the afternoon, they fled northeast again, passing through Fengjiapo, Chenguantou, Donghaizhuang, and at 3:00 PM, they were in the areas of Ligou, Yongjin Temple, Haizhuang, Yuezhuang, Yinjia Guanzhuang, and Suguanzhuang, still fleeing northeast toward Fengshan. A small group fled southeast from Simadianzi in the west of Yishui County, returned to Zhujiazhuang, Linjiazhuang, and Xinglongdian, and after arriving at Sucun at 8:00 AM, fled southeast again, passed Yunshan Shengmuzong, and had returned to the vicinity of Xiazhuang south of Ju County City by noon, still fleeing east. The current goal of the Liu bandits still seems to be to flee into Jiangsu Province again. After the Liu bandits escaped, the suppression troops were ordered to pursue and suppress them overnight. Chairman Han Fuqu also ordered Gao Lantian's department, the 172nd regiment of the 86th brigade of the 29th division stationed in Jiaozhou, to proceed to Zhucheng in preparation for blocking the bandits.

According to the news obtained last night (the 9th), Ma Guanyi's brigade had arrived in Yishui, Li Xuande's cavalry regiment had arrived south of Sucun, Sun Tongxuan's division had arrived in Linyi, and Gu Liangmin's division's direct teams had also arrived in Linyi, while Xue's regiment arrived in Xiazhuang and Tian's regiment arrived in Tangtou Town. It is heard that Han believes that the Lunan area is all mountains, and the Liu bandits are extremely cunning, making encirclement and suppression difficult. He intends to change the plan, only dispatching considerable troops to pursue and suppress them, and deploying heavy troops in key passes between Linyi, Ju County, Yishui, Zhucheng, Rizhao, and Mengyin, to meet and suppress them everywhere, waiting at leisure to quickly eliminate them.

Measures in Guangdong Province to Maintain Paper Currency 115

Guangzhou Correspondence: The Guangdong Provincial Bank's paper currency has been experiencing a low discount trend for several months now. Although the Provincial Bank has stopped exchanging ten-yuan banknotes and adopted measures to seal up shop rental income to reduce the circulation of paper currency in the market, the shop rental income sealed up a month ago has reached its term and has been unsealed one after another. The symptomatic methods of maintaining the paper currency have come to an end, and the one-yuan and five-yuan silver banknotes have still not returned to full circulation. At the same time, some silver industry market brokers are taking this opportunity to openly trade, with different market prices every day. The value of one-yuan and five-yuan silver banknotes is often between ninety percent. The wages earned by the middle and lower-class people through hard work are invisibly reduced to ninety percent each month. On the merchants' side, unwilling to suffer the loss of low discounts, they have to raise prices to compensate for the low discounts on paper currency. The suffering is all transferred to the general public, and the poor are especially affected. Recently, the authorities have seen this and have been discussing ways to maintain the situation for several days. It has been decided to borrow from large merchants in the province and raise 5 million yuan in cash so that the Provincial Bank can fully exchange paper currency as much as possible. On the one hand, silver shops are prohibited from opening to buy and sell. With no one manipulating the market and the Provincial Bank resuming full exchange, it would not be difficult for the discounted paper currency to immediately restore its full value. This is a fundamental maintenance measure. It is understood that the procedures for borrowing a large sum of money are currently being negotiated separately. It is planned to temporarily borrow 1.5 million yuan from tobacco merchants, 1.5 million yuan from a certain merchant, and another 2 million yuan from the prize-winning association contractor as a reserve. As for the 3 million yuan borrowed from the above two merchants, it will be guaranteed by additional tax revenues and increased agricultural taxes, to be repaid within the year. The Provincial Bank will provide interest at the ordinary rate. As for the 5 million yuan borrowed, it will be allowed to be delivered in paper currency. According to Provincial Bank staff, the paper currency currently circulating in the market is no more than 13 million yuan. If the Provincial Bank borrows 5 million yuan in paper currency, then there will only be about 7 million yuan of paper currency remaining in the market. With such a sudden decrease in the amount of paper currency on the market, the restoration of the original value of the paper currency can be realized immediately. As for the government's future repayment of the loans, it is reported that there are already concrete measures in place. The so-called additional tax revenue can increase revenue by about 900,000 yuan per month, and at least 700,000 yuan. In addition, increasing agricultural taxes can increase revenue by 400,000 yuan per month, totaling over 1.2 million yuan per month. Within four months, there will be over 5 million yuan to repay the creditor merchants, which is more than enough. Currently, there is already some progress on this matter. If there are no unexpected obstacles, a loan contract will be signed with the merchants, and the Provincial Bank's paper currency can begin to be fully exchanged at the same time. (April 6th)

Feng Yuxiang's Difficult Situation 116

The Central Government Has Subsidized Him Three Times with 50,000 Yuan

More Than a Thousand Guards Returned to Han Fuqu for Maintenance

Tai'an Correspondence: Commissioner Feng Yuxiang has lived in Tai'an since he left Chahar in August of last year and settled in Shandong again, and it has been more than half a year. He lives by reading and practicing calligraphy every day, and his attitude is quite passive. However, his economic situation is extremely difficult. In the past, Committee Member Huang (郛) had subsidized Feng Yuxiang's living expenses three times for 50,000 yuan. The first time was 20,000 yuan, the second time was also 20,000 yuan, and the third time was 10,000 yuan. In addition, Shandong Provincial Government Chairman Han Fuqu and Chahar Chairman Song Zheyuan provided occasional subsidies. However, Feng's guards in Tai'an still number one to two thousand, and the food costs are high, so he really feels unable to maintain them. Therefore, recently the soldiers only have food to eat, and the officers only receive subsidies of 10 yuan. The poor situation can be imagined. In early December of last year, Feng telegraphed Chahar Province Chairman Song Zheyuan, willing to return the guards to Chahar Province. Subsequently, Liu Ruming, the former division commander of the Northwest Army, was sent to Lu to take them back, preparing to lead Feng's guards back to Chahar. However, Feng's guards resolutely refused to leave Feng, so it could not be realized. Recently, Feng, still unable to secure the guards' salaries, sent Ming Zhexi and Li Xin to Jinan to meet with Chairman Han Fuqu, requesting that more than a thousand guards be handed over to the Third Route Army for all maintenance. Han Fuqu had no choice but to agree, and it is heard that he has agreed to temporarily have Wu Huawen, the brigade commander of the pistol brigade, maintain the status quo of Feng's guards. Approximately within days, he will send personnel to Tai'an to inspect them, and all military salaries will be temporarily subsidized by the Third Central Army. (7th)

The Yuanbei small steamer, which travels between Suzhou City and Dongting West Mountain, left Suzhou for West Mountain on the 8th. When it arrived at the Wangmu Gate of Taihu Lake at about 4:00 PM, the wind and waves were very strong. A ferryboat towed behind the steamer was in great danger. Seven passengers on the ferryboat boarded the steamer one after another to take shelter from the wind. At this time, the ferryboat was overturned by the wind. The boat owner, Zhou Zhaoda, and his wife, Yao, both fell into the river. Fortunately, Zhou Zhaoda was good at swimming and escaped unharmed. After Yao fell into the river, the gale was even stronger, and she tragically drowned. The body was also swept away by the waves. Efforts were made to salvage the body, but no trace was found.

(Wuxi)

Questioning of Civil Affairs Department Staff in the Gu Case 120

Since the incident of Liu Zhuomin's refusal to hand over the case, involving Li Shuyun, the wife of former Director of the Civil Affairs Department, Gu Renfa, and leading to various cases of Gu Renfa's bigamy and fraudulent marriage, as well as Gu Renfa's resignation due to his self-awareness of unease in his position, etc., have been recorded in this newspaper. It is now learned that the County Court Procuratorate recently ordered the summoning of Zeng Fanrong (Binqiu, Sichuan), an inspector of the Civil Affairs Department, Hao Ruyuan (Shanxi), an accountant, and Huang Xutan, the director of Junhe Firm, for interrogation. Yesterday was the court date for this case. Only Zeng and Hao appeared as summoned, while Huang Xutan remained absent. At 2 p.m., Chief Judge Qian opened the court, and the questioning was extremely simple. First, Zeng was asked whether a woman surnamed Li had come to the Civil Affairs Department around March 20th to see Gu Renfa, and whether he had arranged the meeting. Zeng testified that he had arranged the meeting, and that Li came because she wanted to seek a position. Next, Hao Ruyuan was questioned whether a long-distance phone call from Nanjing to the Civil Affairs Department at the end of March was received by him. Hao testified that it was. After the interrogation, they were both ordered to return home. As for Gu Renfa himself, Chief Judge Qian, considering his failure to appear after being summoned twice, which constituted contempt of court, has decided to issue a third summons, ensuring that he appears in court for questioning. According to Hao Ruyuan's statement to reporters, Gu Renfa's personal seal was hung on his belt year-round, never leaving his person. Therefore, the Gu Renfa private seal found on the stationery of the Provincial Residence in Liu Zhuomin's luggage must be a forgery. From this, it can be seen that Gu Renfa's accusation that Li Shuyun stole his seal and sold official positions is also impossible. Furthermore, Mr. Hao also said that the newspaper's reports were mostly based on Li Shuyun's one-sided statements, because Gu Renfa had not treated Li Shuyun unfairly. When Shuyun was in Zhenjiang, Gu had given her 300 yuan per month for living expenses, and so on. It is also heard that this matter initially arose from a misunderstanding. When the Liu Zhuomin case broke out, Liu's wife, Wen Rongzhen, publicly claimed to be like sisters with Li Shuyun, seemingly unafraid. After receiving a report, Chen Guofu, Chairman of Jiangsu Province, believed that Li Shuyun's interference in administrative affairs was a disgrace to official conduct. Therefore, he sent a secret telegram to Gu Renfa, who was in Jiangxi for training, roughly saying, "You should ask your family elder to strictly discipline her, and not let her run around everywhere." Upon receiving the telegram, Gu immediately became angry and telegraphed Chairman Chen, requesting punishment for himself, and ordering his subordinates in the Civil Affairs Department to bring Li back to Zhenjiang for control. Initially, there was no intention to send her and her daughter to the judiciary for interrogation. However, a close confidant of Gu Renfa dispatched by the Civil Affairs Department, named Mr. Zhang Si, hoping to gain great merit, misunderstood Gu's intentions and mobilized a large number of troops, alarming the police and sending them to the court, which made it impossible to bring them back for control, and the case also expanded. Yesterday, Li Wenhui, Li Shuyun's uncle, came to Wuxi to collect the items sent by Shuyun from the detention center. According to talks, external rumors of reconciliation with Gu were strongly denied by Shuyun, whose attitude was resolute. Regarding the accusation of Gu's bigamy, it will be decided after careful consideration after Shuyun recovers from her illness.

The central government has long intended to abolish the Huaibei salt ticket, but after efforts by the transport merchants to save it, it has not been realized until now. Zhenjiang

Jiangsu Construction Department Expands Provincial Long-Distance Telephone 125

The Jiangsu Provincial Department of Construction has drafted organizational regulations for the Long-Distance Telephone Engineering Team and two temporary engineering teams for expanding long-distance telephones north of the Yangtze River. The proposal has been submitted to the provincial government meeting. It has been learned that the organizational regulations are as follows: Article 1: During the construction period of the Jiangsu Construction Department's expansion of state-owned long-distance telephones, an engineering team will be established, and a chief engineer will be appointed, concurrently held by a technical specialist from this department, to manage all technical matters of the engineering teams. Article 2: The engineering team may be increased or decreased depending on the engineering needs. Article 3: Each team will have an engineer and an assistant engineer, appointed by the Construction Department. Article 4: Each team will have two to three clerks, two to three supervisors, appointed by the chief engineer and reported to the Construction Department for record. Article 5: The engineer will, under the orders of the chief engineer, preside over all facilities, management reports, and other matters related to the line project. The assistant engineer, supervisor, and clerk will be under the command of the engineer and handle construction, transportation, storage, accounting, and other matters. Article 6: Each team will have a foreman, several skilled workers, and unskilled workers will be hired locally and paid daily. Article 7: The supervisor and clerk must fill out a report on the daily work progress and submit it to the engineer for verification and forwarding to the chief engineer for record. Article 8: The engineering team shall prepare a report on the progress of the project, together with charts, and submit it once every ten days. Article 9: The engineering team will be dissolved when the project is completed. Article 10: These regulations will be submitted to the provincial government for record and implementation.

County Government Clerk Extorts Money and is Detained 128

Xi Tongfa, a villager in Baoshan Township, the first district, hid elsewhere last year to avoid conscription. Zhang Guirong, a clerk in the Judicial Office of the county government, learned of this and, posing as a trainer from the First District Regiment Department, went to Xi Tongfa to threaten him, saying that he needed to pay 60 yuan to avoid conscription. After repeated pleas, the amount was reduced to 35 yuan, and 20 yuan was paid. Later, another 7 yuan was paid, leaving 8 yuan unpaid. Unexpectedly, the First District Regiment Department recently learned of this matter. After verification, it was found to be true, and a report was submitted to the county government for investigation. County Magistrate Zhang was greatly angered by the report and issued a handwritten order yesterday (the 8th), suspending Zhang Guirong from his duties and placing him under surveillance for strict investigation.

Jiashan

Illegal Levying of Donations by the Ship Office 129

The County Chamber of Commerce of this county, jointly with Ni Shuxiang, a resident of the border of Suzhou, and Shen Xiaoguan, a farmer of Xitang, reported that the Sixth Branch of the Ship Management Office stationed in the third district illegally levied donations, causing constant harm to farmers. For example, when Ni Shuxiang used his own farm boat to carry a sick person to Shan for medical treatment last month, it was already dusk. Suddenly, someone in uniform shouted to stop the boat and went straight into the boat. At first, he said to donate five yuan, nine jiao, and nine fen. After Ni and others begged bitterly, he said he would reduce it by one yuan. After begging again, he said three yuan, nine jiao, and nine fen was the minimum amount. The boatman and the sick person in the boat had a total of three people, carrying only about two yuan, which was only for medical expenses and food. They had no choice but to pay him everything. He still detained the boat and did not release it, forcing them to mortgage the cotton quilt to a shop, paying a total of three yuan and two jiao and four fen, before giving them four licenses, and saying that there were still seven jiao and five fen missing. After paying it off, two boat plates were given. After checking, the four licenses stated a total of three yuan, three jiao, and one fen. After paying the amount, there were still seven fen missing, and they even detained the boat plate and forced them to pay seven jiao and five fen, causing Ni Shuxiang and others on the boat to be hungry and cold, in extreme suffering, forcing them to mortgage the cotton quilt, showing no compassion for the sick person, which was even more inhumane. Not only do farmers directly suffer from it, but merchants also indirectly suffer from it. After receiving the report, the County Chamber of Commerce immediately forwarded it to the Construction Department. It is now learned that the Construction Department has clearly ordered the county to investigate and prohibit it.

Hefei

Resolution of the Sixth Middle School Strike 130

The students of the senior high school and junior high school departments of the Hefei Provincial Sixth Middle School believed that the order from the Education Department to suspend spring vacation did not conform to the usual practice. They unanimously requested the school authorities to grant the vacation as usual, but their request was not approved. As a result, a strike occurred yesterday. Considering the seriousness of the matter, the school urgently telegraphed a report to the Education Department. The Education Department believed that there was an intention to resist the order and telegraphed to strictly investigate the ringleaders. The authorities of the Sixth Middle School identified 11 senior high school students and 5 junior high school students who took the initiative. On the 5th, a notice was posted expelling these 16 students from school. At the same time, the remaining senior and junior high school students were ordered to resume classes uniformly on the 5th.

Jinan

Shandong Yellow River Actively Repairs Dykes in Spring 131

Since Shandong Province suffered a major flood last year, the counties in western Shandong have not yet recovered from the damage. Therefore, the province is taking the Yellow River's spring dyke repair project within the province very seriously this year. The provincial government had previously decided to allocate 300,000 yuan to fund the spring dyke repair. The upstream levee has not seen water for many years, and the levee body is extremely weak. The River Affairs Bureau is paying close attention to this area for this year's spring dyke repair. Pan Yifen, the chief of the engineering section of the bureau, went to the area to survey and supervise the work and returned to Jinan today. According to Pan's statement, the project of adding grass and thickening the entire levee is extremely important and is currently underway, which is expected to be completed in about May. In addition, there are many places in the middle reaches where the local dykes and dams are damaged, and there are many places in the downstream reaches where the dykes and dams need to be repaired. He must inspect and supervise the repair one by one to ensure that it is completed before the major flood to resist the flood.

Shanghai-Woosung Garrison Command Strictly Prohibits Strikes and Slowdowns 132

The Capitalist Side Should Also Not Engage in Abuse

Central News Agency reports, the Shanghai-Woosung Garrison Command announced yesterday, "This city is an important industrial and commercial area, and labor-capital disputes occur from time to time, which is detrimental to the future of industry. Moreover, at a time of national crisis, the entire country should unite and strive to produce and enrich national strength. If the labor and capital sides are allowed to have conflicts from time to time, it will not only reduce the country's due production but also endanger social order, which is a disaster. The duty of this command is to maintain the locality. For this reason, it is announced to all industrial and commercial people that the labor and capital sides share prosperity and adversity and are closely related. Factory owners should usually care for workers and not allow abuse, etc., and workers should work hard for their factories and should not arbitrarily slow down or strike to coerce factory owners, etc. Only in this way can both sides coordinate and expect good results in the process of industrial development. Recently, an order has been received from Chairman Chiang that if factories in various places arbitrarily strike or slow down in the future, the local competent authorities shall strictly prohibit them. If the workers who caused the above-mentioned unrest have a union, the competent authorities may also check the provisions of item 3 of Article 37 of the Trade Union Law and first order the trade union to be dissolved so that the unrest can be resolved quickly. This is an unprecedented example during the national crisis. As for the factory owners, they should not abuse the workers, and the competent authorities should pay special attention at any time and correct them in order to eliminate the invisible, etc. This command has the responsibility and will abide by the previous order if the above-mentioned situation occurs. It is hoped that the industrial and commercial people of this city will take the heart of mutual assistance and the policy of common prosperity, and unite to increase production and enrich national strength. This is our earnest expectation." This announcement is by Commander Wu Tiecheng.

There are rumors that the various yarn mills of Chinese merchants will be managed by the banking community because the yarn mills cannot repay the loans, and the Japanese are taking the opportunity to seize management rights 136

Dagon News Agency reports that for many years, Chinese-owned yarn mills have borrowed money from the banking community to maintain their operations due to poor business conditions. However, according to the current situation, Chinese-owned yarn mills may not be able to repay the loans from the banking community as scheduled. According to people in the yarn industry, the latest situation is recorded below:

The recession of Chinese-owned yarn mills

Due to poor business conditions and more than half of the capital losses, the Chinese-owned yarn mills in this city had no choice but to mortgage the factory and borrow a large amount of money from the banking community, totaling 120 million yuan. After borrowing this money, it was used to revitalize the yarn mill, but recently, due to the impact of the global economic recession, it has been impossible to repay this debt, so many yarn mills are said to be transferred to the management of the banking community. The Japanese are taking the opportunity to seize the management rights of the factory.

The banking community's investment in Chinese-owned yarn mills is purely to develop China's industry and relieve unemployed workers, but recently it has reached such a point that they have to think of other ways to recover this loan. However, the banking community are all laymen when it comes to managing yarn mills, so recently the Japanese have been actively engaged in negotiating with the banking community to have Japanese personnel serve as managers of the factory, but whether it can become a reality is still a question. The banks that invested in Chinese-owned yarn mills are the Bank of China, Bank of Communications, Ningpo Commercial & Savings Bank, Zhejiang Industrial Bank, and other banks.

After the Disappearance of the Sikorsky Aircraft, Search and Rescue Efforts Launched by Land, Sea, and Air; No Concrete Leads Found as of 7 PM; Not Entirely Giving Up Hope, Search Continues 138

Shen Shi News Agency reports that the China National Aviation Corporation's Sikorsky aircraft, which departed for Guangzhou early the previous morning, suddenly went missing. Since yesterday morning, the company has dispatched personnel in three directions – land, sea, and air – to conduct simultaneous and intensive searches. Due to continued adverse weather conditions, as of 7 PM yesterday, according to reports from various sources, the aircraft had still not been located. General speculation suggests that the aircraft's fate is likely more ill-fated than fortunate. Currently, the company is continuing its efforts to search and rescue. The Shen Shi News Agency reporter has learned the following details:

Search and Rescue Efforts Launched by Land, Sea, and Air

The Shanghai-Guangzhou route's number 16 Sikorsky aircraft departed at 7 AM the previous morning. Half an hour later, it was declared missing. On the same day, the China National Aviation Corporation dispatched aircraft twice for searching, but to no avail. Starting yesterday morning, they dispatched personnel in three directions – land, sea, and air – to conduct search and rescue efforts. (1) The company dispatched staff members Wang Heling, Yao Qinru, etc., who hired a car from Shanghai to travel along the Minhang long-distance route to the Xiapu area for detailed inquiries. (2) The company dispatched Nie Kaiyi, deputy director of the flight crew, along with Wang Chengming, a staff member of the crew, who took a Jianghai Customs steamer from the Huangpu River and searched along the Huangpu River towards Wusongkou, splitting up along the way. (3) At noon yesterday, when the heavy fog slightly dissipated, they dispatched two aircraft, a Lockheed and a Sikorsky, which departed one after another at 12:30 PM to search southwards.

Search Yields No Trace

The customs steamer departed at 12 PM and arrived at Hangzhou Bay at 5 PM. According to a telegram to the company, they found no trace of the aircraft along the way. The land personnel had not reported any news as of 6 PM. These personnel will not return to Shanghai until there is a result, in order to continue the detailed search along the way. The dispatched aircraft sent a telegram to the company at around 7 PM, stating that they had also not seen any trace of the aircraft. The aircraft will spend the night in the Xisha Islands and will continue searching early this morning, and requested that another aircraft be dispatched to assist in the search. The company and the families of the pilots are extremely anxious. However, according to pilots who returned to Shanghai after the search, the aircraft may have landed on the sea surface. If there are no further results, a warship will be dispatched to search the sea surface. The pilots and passengers on board the aircraft are:

According to the China National Aviation Corporation's announcement, the missing aircraft included two American pilots: the main pilot, Robert L. Gest, and the co-pilot, Jamos Finek. Finek had only been in Shanghai for two months. In addition, there was one passenger, a manager of a certain Japanese export trading company, who was flying to Fuzhou on the aircraft. Yesterday, Manager Dai of the company told a Shen Shi News Agency reporter that, regarding this aircraft's disappearance, the company, as its duty lies, will make its greatest efforts to search for its whereabouts. If it is not found in one day, the search will not be abandoned for a single day. A detailed report has now been sent to the ministry.

American-Asiatic Factory Workers Surround the Social Affairs Bureau, Police Dispatched Yesterday to Disperse Them; Leading Trouble-Making Workers Detained and Sent to Police Headquarters for Interrogation; Party and Government Jointly Issue a Proclamation Ordering Workers to Resume Work; Factory to Comply with Orders and Resume Operations Normally Starting This Morning; Municipal Federation of Trade Unions Issues a Letter to American-Asiatic Factory Workers 139

All workers of the American-Asiatic Silk Weaving Factory went on strike to protest the factory's reduction of wages. The Social Affairs Bureau convened both parties for mediation the day before yesterday, but failed. All workers went to the Social Affairs Bureau one after another starting at 1 PM, ostensibly to petition, but in reality surrounded the bureau. They did not disperse the whole night before last. It was not until yesterday noon that the Security Department and the Public Security Bureau jointly dispatched police to disperse them, and arrested eleven leading workers who were stirring up trouble, sending them to the Garrison Headquarters for interrogation. Party and government organs issued a joint

proclamation, ordering the workers to resume work. The Silk Weavers' Federation of Trade Unions also issued a letter to the American-Asiatic workers, urging them to resume work and await a resolution. The details of each item are recorded below:

Petitioning Workers Dispersed by Police

All workers of the American-Asiatic Factory went to the Social Affairs Bureau in the city center one after another to petition, starting at 1 PM the day before yesterday.

The number of people reached five or six hundred. They put forward two demands: (1) Maintain workers' meals; (2) Stop reducing wages. Xu Yefu of the Social Affairs Bureau, together with Long Peiyun, a representative of the Municipal Party Committee, and Wang Guoxian, a representative of the Public Security Bureau, persuaded the crowd and expressed acceptance of the requests. However, the workers insisted on an immediate resolution and refused to leave, surrounding the doors of the Social Education Bureau and the Hygiene Bureau, preventing bureau staff from entering and leaving. Extending until the evening, the workers gathered in increasing numbers, reaching more than two thousand by about 11 PM the night before last. They still did not disperse until dawn, and shouted slogans, intending to break into the bureau and carry out destruction. Mayor Wu, upon receiving the report, believed that the workers dared to cause trouble by gathering a crowd and surrounding government offices, which clearly indicated that there were reactionary elements instigating them. He immediately ordered the Security Department and the Public Security Bureau to dispatch police to disperse them. Director Yang and Director Wen, upon receiving the order, immediately ordered the police brigade's third squadron, led by He An, and soldiers, all carrying bamboo poles, and prepared two fire trucks, to rush to the city center at 8 AM yesterday to disperse the workers. Because there were many workers, the order was disrupted for a while, and several people were squeezed and injured. Among them, two women and one man were seriously injured and were immediately sent to the Hygiene Bureau for treatment. It was not until about 11 AM that the workers gradually dispersed. Bureau staff, who had been surrounded for a day and a night, were finally able to go out, and were all exhausted.

Leading Trouble-Making Workers Detained and Sent to Police Headquarters

Mayor Wu believed that the workers dared to cause trouble by gathering a crowd, which was obviously disrupting public order and was close to being reactionary. In addition to ordering the Security Department and the Public Security Bureau to dispatch police to disperse them, he also ordered the Seventh District's Second Precinct to detain eleven worker representatives who were stirring up trouble. After being sent to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for interrogation, they were immediately transferred to the Garrison Headquarters for legal proceedings. Their names are as follows: Huang Baofu, Cai Shoufu (Factory 1), Feng Xianchun (Factory 2), Xia Zhiwei (Factory 3), Lü Haiquan (Factory 4), female worker Zhu Linchai (Factory 5), Cai Hangsong (Factory 6), He Yayun (Factory 7), Tong Chunqi (Factory 8), female worker Liu Yanqing (Factory 9), Pan Yuancai (Factory 10).

Mayor Wu Issues Statement Yesterday

Mayor Wu, regarding the American-Asiatic Silk Weaving Factory workers' petition at the Social Affairs Bureau the day before yesterday, which did not disperse overnight, believed that the actions were excessive and disregarded the law. He specifically issued a statement yesterday, saying that after the dispute occurred at the American-Asiatic Silk Weaving Factory, the municipal government ordered the Social Affairs Bureau to investigate the truth and, together with the Municipal Party Committee, to properly mediate. However, the workers were incited by malicious elements, gathered to occupy the Social Affairs Bureau, and refused to disperse, obstructing official duties. The actions were excessive and disregarded the law, which was truly unacceptable. According to reports, there were indeed people who were not workers manipulating and directing from within. The municipal government, considering that the workers were simple-minded, sought to resolve the matter in a roundabout way and was unwilling to punish them by law. Those who incited and instigated have been ordered to be investigated and arrested. Regarding the labor-capital dispute, the matter should be resolved after awaiting proper arrangements by the party and government organs. In recent years, the city has been affected by the current situation, and all industries are in decline. It is appropriate to strive for production and strengthen our forces. Both labor and capital should understand each other during this period and not create misunderstandings. Chairman Chiang's recent telegram also earnestly advised that labor and capital should be interdependent and must cooperate. Factory owners and workers should all abide by this.

Wage Reduction Issue to Be Handled Continuously

According to a person in charge of the Social Affairs Bureau who spoke to a Dagong News Agency reporter, regarding the issue of wage reduction at the American-Asiatic Factory, the Social Affairs Bureau has decided to continue handling the matter in accordance with the law. Although the factory claimed that it had been shut down for a long time and its economic turnover was sluggish, requesting to be declared bankrupt, the Social Affairs Bureau still ordered it to resume operations as usual and maintain workers' meals in order to avoid inciting accidents and causing major disputes. As for the workers, if there are any further acts of resistance and trouble-making, they will be dealt with severely in order to maintain local order.

Party and Government Proclamation Orders Resumption of Work

The Shanghai Special Municipal Executive Committee of the Chinese Kuomintang and the Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau issued a joint proclamation yesterday, ordering the workers to resume work, stating that the decline of China's silk industry has not been a matter of a single day. The American-Asiatic Silk Weaving Factory in the city, with its relatively large capital, has been able to maintain itself with great effort amid the industry's precarious situation. The workers working in the factory should remember the spirit of being in the same boat and share the difficulties together. However, during this wage reduction dispute, while the Social Affairs Bureau was convening a mediation committee, the factory workers still gathered to cause trouble in the name of petitioning. Such disregard for the facts and the expansion of the dispute clearly indicates that there are reactionary elements instigating them. If the labor-capital dispute leads the factory to a point of no return, wouldn't it be a situation of mutual harm? In addition to the wage reduction dispute still being mediated in accordance with the law, and ordering the factory to resume operations as usual, a special joint proclamation is issued, ordering all workers of the factory to comply, resume work on the specified date, work with peace of mind, and be careful not to be exploited by others to test the law. Be vigilant and do not violate this order. Sincerely, this proclamation, dated April, 23rd year of the Republic of China. Standing Committee Members Pan Gongzhan, Wu Xingya, Tong Xingbai. Director Wu Xingya.

Factory Claims Meal Supply Never Disrupted

According to a person in charge of the factory, all factories have never disrupted meal supply. Factories 4, 10, and 7 are still providing meals as usual. However, the welfare workers who manage the meals in each factory have been repeatedly detained, beaten, and humiliated by the workers. Tea, water, and food have also been unable to enter. Their suffering is extreme. Ma Bole, the factory director of Factory 4, was even detained by the workers for a day and a night. He was rescued by police officers from the Sixth District's Security Bureau before he was able to escape. Therefore, the welfare workers are extremely fearful for the safety of their own lives and were only able to escape when the workers went to the city center to surround the Social Affairs Bureau. They are unwilling to continue to return to work. Currently, each factory has rice and firewood in reserve, and the cooks are still remaining in the factory. There should be no problem with the workers' meals. The factory is now trying its best to persuade the welfare workers to return to the factory to work.

Factories to Resume Operations Today in Compliance with Orders

The American-Asiatic Silk Weaving General Company, in order to comply with the orders of the party and government organs to resume operations immediately, has decided to make efforts to resume operations starting today. The general company has notified all branch factories to sound the whistle and resume operations as usual this morning, urging the workers to enter the factory and resume work. The party and government are deeply concerned that accidents may occur temporarily, so they have notified the Municipal Public Security Bureau to dispatch police to protect each factory. The factories in the concession areas have also been notified to the concession authorities for the same protection.

Federation of Trade Unions' Letter to American-Asiatic Workers

The Municipal Federation of Trade Unions issued a letter to all workers of the American-Asiatic Factory yesterday, stating that, beloved workers of the American-Asiatic Factory, in today's China, under the continuous aggression of imperialism, the rural economy is on the verge of bankruptcy, and industrial and commercial enterprises are becoming increasingly depressed. The entire country is in a precarious situation. The imperialists are taking advantage of our danger to intensify their political aggression and implement dumping policies to carry out economic aggression. China's fledgling industry and commerce, after this major blow, and because of the social and economic depression, are increasingly trapped in a dangerous situation. News of factory closures and wage reductions is heard from all over the country, and the number of unemployed workers is rapidly increasing, forming a major domestic panic today. In this crisis, how should our labor and capital maintain each other, cooperate sincerely, break through this difficulty, and survive this difficult situation together? However, a few capitalists who are ignorant of the situation are still unable to awaken and continue to follow their habitual techniques of oppressing workers, creating unnecessary disputes. There are also some unscrupulous elements who disregard the current crisis and carry out their methods of sowing discord, inciting workers to indulge their ability to cause trouble, leading to major disputes between labor and capital. This is what the federation deeply regrets. The American-Asiatic Silk Factory, under the pretext that the silk industry is extremely depressed and business cannot be maintained, suddenly announced a wage reduction without submitting it to the party and government organs for approval, causing the workers' lives to be affected. The process is indeed inappropriate. Our workers announced a strike to seek self-preservation, and the federation expresses its deep sympathy. Maintaining the strike until now has lasted for a month. The federation is particularly concerned about the suffering of the workers' lives during the strike period. Now that the case has been mediated by the party and government organs in accordance with the law, the workers should share the difficulties together, be in the same boat, resume work on the specified date, and await a solution. This way, the future of the industry will not go bankrupt, and their own livelihoods will be spared from being affected. Do not be exploited by others to cause further incidents. This is what the federation sincerely hopes for.

Construction Committee Negotiates Electricity Loan with Banking Syndicate; Total Loan Amount is Three Million Yuan; Secured by Continued Issuance of Electricity Public Bonds 140

Shen Shi News Agency reports that the Capital Construction Committee recently negotiated with the Shanghai banking community to borrow three million yuan for electricity projects, for the development of the Capital Electric Plant, the Qishuyan Electric Plant, and the Huainan Mining Bureau. After a month of negotiations, it has now been completely successful. The Shen Shi News Agency reporter has recorded the details as follows:

Use of Loan

The Capital Electric Plant, the Qishuyan Electric Plant, and the Huainan Mining Bureau are all projects directly managed by the Construction Committee. Although the scale is not very small, due to a lack of funds and sluggish turnover, development is difficult. The three million yuan borrowed from the Shanghai banking syndicate is expected to be allocated as follows: (1) Capital Electric Plant: 1.2 million yuan; (2) Qishuyan Electric Plant: 600,000 yuan; (3) Huainan Mining Bureau: 1.2 million yuan, for a total of 3 million yuan.

Hope for Projects

According to a certain high-ranking official who represented the Construction Committee in the loan negotiations, the loan has now been fully established and the procedures have been agreed upon. In the future, this loan will be used to develop the following: (1) The Capital Electric Plant can increase its generating capacity by 10,000 kilowatts, and the necessary transmission, distribution, and user equipment can be improved according to plan. (2) The Qishuyan Electric Plant is the main hub for supplying power to the industries of Changzhou and Wuxi, and its position is particularly important. In the future, with improved equipment and increased capacity, the cost of electricity for each factory can be reduced, alleviating the burden on factories. This is a fundamental plan for developing industry and commerce. (3) The Huainan Mining Bureau was established in April 1930. The mining area is located in Shungeng Mountain, Huaiyuan, Anhui. Currently, it can only produce 7-8 tons of bituminous coal per day. After the loan is successful, new-style machinery will be purchased, and the daily output can be increased to 1,200 tons. Within two years, the estimated daily output can reach 3,000 tons. The coal quality is excellent, and the mineral resources are abundant, making it a promising mine.

Lending Banks

The amount of this loan is a total of three million yuan. The lending banks include twelve institutions: the Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, the Shanghai Bank, the China & South Sea Bank, the Jin Cheng Bank, the Yien Yieh Commercial Bank, the Continental Bank, the Zhejiang Industrial Bank, the Ningpo Commercial Bank, the Kwang Hua Commercial Bank, the China Agricultural and Industrial Bank, and the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau. The Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, and the Shanghai Bank contributed the most, accounting for about half of the total. The two parties signed the contract yesterday, using the continued issuance of electricity public bonds as collateral, to be repaid in three years. The banking syndicate has designated the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications as representative banks to be responsible for receipts and payments. The funds are being paid in installments.
