Novel

Siamese Ramblings (10) 279

— Yi Min

The year before last was the heyday of Chinese education in Siam. The opening of secondary schools, the establishment of kindergartens, the holding of joint academic competitions among schools, and large-scale joint sports meets all caused a sensation for a while. A kind of enthusiastic and lively atmosphere permeated the entire Siamese Chinese community. But soon it suffered an unexpected blow, and that was the so-called compulsory education ordinance promulgated by the Siamese government.

Originally, compulsory education exists in all countries, but the regulations promulgated by Siam last year broke the usual international customs. They not only limited the children of this country to receive this education, but also included our overseas Chinese children in the compulsory list. In other words, we must abandon the characters of our blessed country to read their Siamese books. It is very obvious that we want to assimilate our three million overseas Chinese! At that time, although the schools had pleaded with them, they finally failed due to internal inconsistencies.

Now, Chinese schools have been changed to teach Siamese language. Only a small number of students who are over the age they specify (over 15 years old) or whose Siamese level is sufficient can read Chinese books. But this is an extremely small number. Therefore, we can say that overseas Chinese education in Siam is now completely bankrupt!

8. Conclusion

At present, the overseas Chinese in Siam are really at a time of great crisis. If we do not find a way to save it, the future is really unimaginable! I think that on the one hand, we must ask the government to quickly sign a treaty with Siam, so that all problems can be solved easily. But more importantly, it is the awakening of the compatriots themselves. As long as everyone abandons local concepts, concentrates talents and economy, and is of one mind, it will not be difficult to return to the golden age before, because Siam is an agricultural country and its industry is still very immature. The manufacture of all daily necessities can be done greatly at present. As for the increased exorbitant taxes of the resident government, we should argue with reason on the one hand, and improve factory management with scientific methods on the other hand to reduce costs. We must never do our duty by eating, and be humble. Speaking of agriculture, what has been reclaimed now is only the alluvial land in the middle and estuary of the Chao Phraya River, which is less than one-tenth of the total area of Siam. The rest of the vast wilderness can also be developed greatly. It is not absolutely impossible to abolish or amend harsh laws such as compulsory education and immigration regulations. In short, the success or failure of overseas Chinese in Siam in the future depends on whether everyone can wake up? (End)

The Making of the "The Good Earth" Film 280

—

The making of the "The Good Earth" film based on Pearl S. Buck's novel has been a matter of much debate for a long time, but now the decision has been made to begin filming. Since Mr. Hill (George W. Hill) led the staff of MGM to Shanghai,

the outside world knows very little about the progress of the "The Good Earth" film. In fact, they have been making rapid progress in collecting materials everywhere for several weeks. Mr. Hill has now announced the progress of the work, and the mystery of the film world has finally been solved.

Mr. Hill is the director of "The Good Earth" film. He strongly advocates taking materials on the spot for this important film, and abandoning all fake scenes. Therefore, he personally traveled thousands of miles to Shanghai, Suzhou, Hangzhou, Nanjing, Beijing, and inland villages. He led the specialist technicians of MGM to capture real backgrounds. The arduousness of the work is beyond the imagination of ordinary people. Someone asked him what was going on? He said, "That's hard to answer. We are filming everything on the spot, from the mattresses of the rich to the farming tools of the farmers."

He also said, "Some people suspect that we are splitting China. In fact, we are indeed collecting everything and preparing to build a miniature China in Hollywood." He also said, "We are not satisfied with just imitation. We bought them and shipped them back to Hollywood. As of now, we have shipped about 190 boxes to Hollywood, and nine-tenths of our work has been completed. After that, we will spend several months completing our set. The "The Good Earth" film may be shown to the world in late autumn this year or early spring next year."

Mr. Hill is quite interested in China and hopes to revisit the old place in a few years. At that time, he plans to rent a houseboat and travel leisurely to the interior of China. In his mind, Beijing is the most worthy of nostalgia in the world. He found that Chinese people are good at cooperation. The National Government has appointed two people to help them, and a dozen wealthy Chinese people are very happy to present their treasures. Therefore, he has a good opportunity to see private collections of gems, ancient bronzes, and luxurious decorations. He admires the essence of China very much. He praised that the Chinese people's etiquette is not a kind of lip service, because sometimes he loves something so much that the owner generously gives it to him.

Pearl S. Buck's novel tells the story from 1906 to the present, and it is all set in China. He said, "We should have Chinese costumes. The protagonists and ordinary actors should wear costumes from one era to another." Therefore, he hired Chinese craftsmen to design patterns for several months. Specialist technicians and photographers spared no effort to capture the real scenery of China, hoping not to lose the life of the Chinese people as described by Pearl S. Buck. They went to Nanjing again yesterday. After a few weeks, they will pack up and return to the United States.

Film reviews

Review of "Little Women" 281

— Luo Ping · Xun Zhi Ling He

"Little Women" 丨 Grand Shanghai 丨

(I)

The protagonist, Yu, in "Little Women" is the author, Louisa May Alcott herself, and everything in "Little Women" is her own experience.

Yes, this novel, a narrative poem of ordinary and trivial American family life, is widely popular. Sixteen years ago, William Brady adapted it into a stage play, and later it was made into a silent film; now, in the era of sound films, it has been remade into a talkie.

This is a world-famous literary work, but not all famous literary works are worth accepting; critical work is needed here.

The exchange between the literary and film worlds is not necessarily a bad phenomenon in modern times. In the impoverished Chinese film scene, marked by the release of "Spring Silkworms," a new path for Chinese literary films has been opened, although it was soon hit. However, it is easy to understand that we cannot casually deceive the audience with "literary films." When film merchants use the original work as a selling point, we should take a more serious attitude to criticize it.

Naturally, "Little Women" has its own considerable value; it depicts the little women of modern society – a group of virtuous wives and good mothers.

This group resents and yet submits to their wealthy aunt; they are filial to their parents, loving to their sisters; they are pleased and grateful for the gifts and favors of the wealthy; they give humane and generous alms to a poor family with a newborn child; they have no ideals or prospects for their future, or want to be a superhuman writer – all this is their life, the so-called "little women" and "good wives."

The author's view of life expressed in "Little Women" is, to put it precisely, just a kind of "philosophy of contentment with poverty." Therefore, the characters in the work are all content with their lot, optimistic, and believe in fate. Their highest goal is to work diligently and earnestly in this society to be a "good person," a good daughter, a good sister, and a good wife. There is poverty, misfortune, and sorrow in this story, but those poor protagonists only show sorrow and obedience, without the slightest thought.

At the same time, the more important point is that in this circle, everyone is a good person. The four sisters go without saying; the parents, Laurie, Brooke, Professor Bhaer, and even the aunt we dislike – within this group, there is absolutely no concept of self-interest or selfish thoughts among them. On the contrary, they only have sympathy, compassion, joy, and gratitude. In other words, these people seem very, very far removed from us. To describe them with a phrase they often use, they are all angels, all superhumans. The original author and the filmmakers have worked hard on this kind of benevolent "self-denial" doctrine. On the contrary, whether in the novel or on the screen, they have very wonderfully presented a picture of harmony. Watching this work will take you to a paradise, a utopia, and make you forget the ugliness and anger of the world. We can sympathize with such good people, and at the same time, people with this kind of goodness do exist in modern society. However, when we sympathize emptily, we will forget the anger of reality. When we are moved by the innocence and kindness of the protagonists in the play and shed tears and give smiles, at this time we will dissipate our sorrow for reality. Advising people to be content with poverty, to restrain themselves, to resolve the resentment accumulated in real society, and to obscure the observation of social problems – these are the objective tasks pursued by the life view of "Little Women."

We must consider the objective performance of the work, and we must see who welcomes the work, and we should be more cautious. The simultaneous public screening of "The Outlaw" and "Little Women" provides us with a good comparison. We believe that "The Outlaw" is far more worthy of praise than "Little Women." If we feel like watching "Little Women" but haven't seen "The Outlaw," then we sincerely and seriously offer a piece of advice to our dear readers – go see "The Outlaw" first!

(II)

"Little Women" is an American home life story. It can be said that the characters in "Little Women" are ordinary American people. Their experiences are also experiences that can happen anytime, anywhere in the United States.

In order to poeticize and beautify this ordinary and trivial story, and "make the audience cry sympathetically and smile knowingly," the filmmakers have worked hardest on the depiction of the environment, and this point has achieved considerable success. The screenwriters (Herrman and Mason) are also very good at deleting cumbersome details and narrating this long story quite smoothly. Of course, here we can only say that they are competent, without special expression. Especially in the part after Meg and Brooke's marriage, it is slightly lax. Afterwards, probably because they were eager to proceed towards the ending, it gradually became disorganized. Of course, the famous acting skills of Hepburn and Paul Lukas saved many of these shortcomings.

The director of "Little Women" is very successful in the delicate and vivid depiction of personality. For example, Yu sold her hair for money, but in the evening, she regretted her lost hair. Yu's innocence and emotional personality are portrayed.

Another point is that the director is very capable of controlling and manipulating the audience's emotions, from joy to sorrow, from sorrow to joy, all depicted appropriately. For example, at the beginning, a group of innocent children are happy, and their mother comes in and tells them that their father has sent a letter. Then, the mother slowly reads the letter, but before the letter is finished, several close-ups show that the daughters are already in tears. This scene is very moving. This technique was used again when they received the telegram about their father's illness. 丨丨 Several places of grief and sorrow in the original work are handled very well. The most outstanding are the sections of Yu selling her hair and Beth's illness. When Beth is critically ill, Mei pretends that sleep is death, deliberately making a shocking stroke, also exerting the ability to manipulate the audience's emotions to the extreme.

The success of most of this play lies in the successful individual performance of Hepburn. Perhaps it can be said that it almost makes us imagine that Alcott's original work was written for her. The whole article is impeccable, this person is Kerr. The great reputation is not easily achieved in vain.

Speaking of acting, Francis Dee's Meg is also very successful. In the section before her engagement, she looks out the window, tidies up her eyebrows in the mirror, sees Yu, is embarrassed, but cannot hide the joy in her heart. After talking to Yu, her fiancé comes in, panting, pretending to be calm, but with a very surprised expression in his heart – one of the daughters will be screened in Nanjing soon.

, indeed, she performed vividly. Lukas' Professor Bhaer is also good.

(III)

Taking this film as an example, we may as well look at the different points between novels and movies. On the one hand, this is because the capacity of about 10,000 feet of film is definitely not as rich as a novel of hundreds of thousands of words, so the entire novel cannot be put on the screen. More importantly, the two have their own unique styles and techniques, so what is expressed on the screen is no longer exactly the same as the novel. Here, we may as well give one or two specific examples.

The first chapter of the original book describes the outline of each person's personality, and the center of the story is the preparation of Christmas gifts for Mama. But on the screen, it first explains the environment at the time, and then individually writes about the business and life of each little girl from Mama down. This visualizes what is said in one or two sentences in the novel, and at the same time, there are differences in the timing.

On Christmas morning, when Mama returns from outside, the dialogue in the original book is:

"Merry Christmas, Mama! Thank you for your books," the four daughters said in unison. "We have read them, and we will read them every day from now on."

"Merry Christmas to you, my children," Mama said. "I am very happy that you have read them, and I hope you will continue to read them. However, I have something to tell you. There is a woman sleeping in the house next door, and there is a newborn child. Six children are huddled together on a bed so that they don't freeze to death, because there is no fire in their house. They have nothing to eat, so her eldest child came to tell me and asked me to help them. My girls, can you give them your breakfast as a Christmas gift?"

"Luckily you came quickly," Yu said. "We haven't eaten it yet."

"May I be allowed to go with you," Beth said. "To distribute these things to those poor children?"

"I'll take the butter and scones," Mei said.

"I know you're willing," the mother said. "You all go and help. When you come back, we'll eat some bread and milk for breakfast, and have a good lunch."

But the dialogue in the movie is as follows:

"Sausage! Where did it come from?" Yu opened the lid and said loudly.

"And scones! Just two for each person," Mei also said happily. Then the eldest daughter, Meg, said:

"And coffee!" Then Beth sighed and said:

"I'm afraid Father doesn't have coffee to drink!"

"I remember," the old maid said. "In those years, there was coffee on your father's table every day." Then Mei said innocently and surprisingly:

"Really? Then we were very rich in the beginning."

At this time, after returning from outside and receiving the gifts from her daughters, she said: "Children, wait a moment, I just came from the house next door. They just had a new baby, and the mother and six children are all sleeping. They are cold and hungry, and they only have one quilt, so they are hugging each other to keep warm. Good daughters, would you be willing to give them your breakfast as a Christmas gift?"·········

From the above examples, we can know the special techniques of movies. Movies do not have to rely on literary psychological descriptions, and the screen must be concise and clear, using action to replace words. Sound movies have strengthened the effect of dialogue, so the personality of each character can be described in the dialogue. For example, Beth said, "I'm afraid Father doesn't have coffee to drink!" can show her gentle and kind nature. Yu's masculinity is expressed in the way she speaks. As for Mei's childish selfishness, it is also expressed in the unwillingness she shows when she finally picks up a pot of vegetables.

Well, in the movie, the playwright has indeed understood the essence of the original work and fully used the techniques of film. On the other hand, if the order of the story is based on the original work and is exactly the same, then the result will inevitably be dull and redundant. Here, it strongly answers Mr. Mu Tian's question of whether "Spring Silkworms" should be the same as the original work. At the same time, in this film, we can learn some screenwriting techniques for literary films.

(IV)

Due to space limitations, we have to stop here. However, for this film that shook America, it is time for a great criticism.

"White Mountains, Black Waters, and a Beautiful Heart" Returns from Hangzhou Filming 282

Xu Xinfu's new film, "White Mountains, Black Waters, and a Beautiful Heart," went to Hangzhou on the third of this month to shoot outdoor scenes. In addition to Xu Xinfu, the team included the film's actors Hu Die, Wang Zhengxin, and the chubby child You Guangzhao, as well as the cinematographer Yan Bingheng. They filmed for three days at places such as the Liuhe Pagoda and the Nine Creeks and Eighteen Gorges in Hangzhou, and the results were satisfactory and the work went smoothly. The team has now returned to Shanghai, and the film "White Mountains, Black Waters, and a Beautiful Heart" has now been completely filmed.

"Abandoned Love" to Open Soon 283

On the 16th at the "Beijing" Theater

The film "Abandoned Love," produced by Guoqiang Film Company, has taken more than three months and cost thousands of yuan since December last year to complete the work of filming and sound recording. The results were satisfactory. It has now been reviewed by the Nanjing Film Censorship Committee and the Shanghai Concession Film Censorship Committee, and is scheduled to premiere at the Beijing Grand Theater on the sixth of this month.

The company is now preparing the second all-sound dialogue film script, "The Zhao Family." It is still directed by Ji Fansan, and written and starred by Zhao Yingcai. The female lead was once recruited, but has now been hired, with Ms. Chen Yin and Ms. Qing Ping taking on the role.

After the Establishment of the Revival Comrades Association, the Mingxing Company Has a New Look 284

Mingxing Company is the earliest and largest film company in the history of Chinese cinema. In recent years, it has been hit by various unexpected setbacks such as the "Romance of Laughter and Tears" disputes, and has fallen into difficult circumstances. Recently, the unexpected success of "Twin Sisters" has made the situation optimistic in all aspects, so it immediately initiated the organization of the "Revival Comrades Association" established on April 1, changing the organization, revising the rules, and giving the internal structure a completely new look.

One of Ai Xia's Posthumous Works 285

"Children of the Times" Passed

Ai Xia has been dead for two months, and her destruction is a great loss to the film industry, but there is no way to bring her back to life, and regret is only futile. Ai Xia's posthumous works that have not been released publicly only include three, namely "Golden Valley," "Children of the Times," and "Two Against One" (talkie). Now "Two Against One" is about to be completed, and "Children of the Times," directed by Li Pingqian, has recently passed the Nanjing Film Censorship Committee.

Recent News of the Silver Screen Little Troublemakers 286

— Zhuang You

A few years ago, we often saw a team of male, female, beautiful, ugly, fat, thin, honest, and cunning child stars in films. They were dedicated to filming comical short films for various companies. They were famous for making trouble. In Hollywood, they often joked and played pranks with the big stars, making the film city turned upside down. So people gave them a nickname called the Silver Screen Little Troublemakers.

Previously, this group of little troublemakers was very young and very smart, so the comedies they starred in were very popular with the audience. But time flies, and now they have all grown up! It is really no longer suitable for them to play those slapstick, troublemaking films, so recently there has been no trace of this group of little troublemakers on the screen! Although a few talented individuals, such as Jackie Cooper, Dick Moore, and Spanky McFarland, have been continuously hired by major companies, most people are ignored. But they all have rich theatrical experience and skills, so how can they be buried like this! So they joined forces and went to New York, preparing to use the stage as a training ground to make a comeback. It is said that they have now been hired by a large theater on Broadway.

The film novel "Sound and Shadow Record" is temporarily suspended for a day or two due to the non-arrival of the sequel manuscript.
